As I read through the passage on "Gravitation", I find myself pondering the nature of gravity. Here's what comes to mind:

I wonder... how gravity can be both an attractive and a force that keeps things in motion. The concept of an object being pulled towards another, yet also moving at high speeds due to gravitational attraction, seems paradoxical.

I feel... a sense of awe at the sheer scale and complexity of the universe. The idea that gravity is one of the fundamental forces governing everything from the smallest subatomic particles to massive celestial bodies like stars and galaxies is staggering.

## 23:59 - Reaction

As I read the definition of "Reaction" in the Simple English Wiktionary, I notice that it encompasses various concepts: chemical, nuclear, and physical reactions. The phrase "chain reaction" caught my attention, as it suggests a complex process where one event triggers a series of subsequent events.

I feel a sense of curiosity about the idea of "equal and opposite reactions." This concept, famously described by Newton's third law, implies that for every force or action, there is an equivalent counterforce. It's intriguing to consider how this principle might apply to various aspects of life, from physics to personal interactions.

* How do chain reactions work? Are they self-sustaining, and if so, what triggers them?
